<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guitar_style">Guitar style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Joni_Mitchell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Guitar style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While some of Mitchell's most popular songs were written on piano, almost every song she composed on the guitar uses an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_tuning" title="Open tuning">open</a>, or non-standard, tuning; she has written songs in some 50 tunings, playing what she has called "Joni's weird chords". The use of alternative tunings allows guitarists to produce accompaniment with more varied and wide-ranging textures. Her right-hand picking/strumming technique has evolved over the years from an initially intricate picking style, typified by the guitar songs on her first album, to a looser and more rhythmic style, sometimes incorporating percussive "slaps".</p>
<p>In 1995, Mitchell's friend Fred Walecki, proprietor of Westwood Music in Los Angeles, developed a solution to alleviate her continuing frustration with using multiple alternative tunings in live settings. Walecki designed a Stratocaster-style guitar to function with the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roland_VG-8&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roland VG-8 (page does not exist)">Roland VG-8</a> virtual guitar, a system capable of configuring her numerous tunings electronically. While the guitar itself remained in standard tuning, the VG-8 encoded the pickup signals into digital signals which were then translated into the altered tunings. This allowed Mitchell to use one guitar on stage, while an off-stage tech entered the preprogrammed tuning for each song in her set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1996_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1996-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mitchell was also highly innovative <a href="/wiki/Harmony" title="Harmony">harmonically</a> in her early work (1966–72) using techniques including <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/modality" title="wikt:modality">modality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromaticism" title="Chromaticism">chromaticism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pedal_point" title="Pedal point">pedal points</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On her 1968 debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Song_to_a_Seagull" title="Song to a Seagull">Song to a Seagull</a></i>, Mitchell used both <a href="/wiki/Quartal_and_quintal_harmony" title="Quartal and quintal harmony">quartal and quintal harmony</a> in "Dawntreader", and she used quintal harmony in <i>Seagull</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003 <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> named her the 72nd greatest guitarist of all time; she was the highest-ranked woman on the list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Joni_Mitchell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mitchell's approach to music struck a chord with many female listeners. In an era dominated by the stereotypical male rock star, she presented herself as "multidimensional and conflicted ... allow[ing] her to build such a powerful identification among her female fans". Mitchell asserted her desire for artistic control throughout her career, and still holds the publishing rights for her music. While she has disclaimed the notion that she is a "feminist", David Shumway notes that "she became the first woman in popular music to be recognized as an artist in the full sense of that term. She rose to popularity at a time when women were still primarily singers of other people's songs and who were marketed almost exclusively on their sex appeal. Though Mitchell undeniably had the latter, it was not what made people buy her records or love her songs. Whatever Mitchell's stated views of feminism, what she represents more than any other performer of her era is the new prominence of women's perspectives in cultural and political life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shumway_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-shumway-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mitchell's work has had an influence on many other artists, including <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Goulding" title="Ellie Goulding">Ellie Goulding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corinne_Bailey_Rae" title="Corinne Bailey Rae">Corinne Bailey Rae</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mikael_%C3%85kerfeldt" title="Mikael Åkerfeldt">Mikael Åkerfeldt</a> from <a href="/wiki/Opeth" title="Opeth">Opeth</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marillion" title="Marillion">Marillion</a> members <a href="/wiki/Steve_Hogarth" title="Steve Hogarth">Steve Hogarth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rothery" title="Steve Rothery">Steve Rothery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> their former vocalist and lyricist <a href="/wiki/Fish_(singer)" title="Fish (singer)">Fish</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Carrack" title="Paul Carrack">Paul Carrack</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haim_(band)" title="Haim (band)">Haim</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>. <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> has also cited Mitchell as the first female artist that really spoke to her as a teenager; "I was really, really into Joni Mitchell. I knew every word to <i><a href="/wiki/Court_and_Spark" title="Court and Spark">Court and Spark</a></i>; I worshipped her when I was in high school. <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_(Joni_Mitchell_album)" title="Blue (Joni Mitchell album)">Blue</a></i> is amazing. I would have to say of all the women I've heard, she had the most profound effect on me from a lyrical point of view."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several artists have had success <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covering</a> Mitchell's songs. <a href="/wiki/Judy_Collins" title="Judy Collins">Judy Collins</a>'s 1967 recording of "Both Sides Now" reached No. 8 on Billboard charts and was a breakthrough in the career of both artists (Mitchell's own recording did not see release until two years later, on her second album <i><a href="/wiki/Clouds_(Joni_Mitchell_album)" title="Clouds (Joni Mitchell album)">Clouds</a></i>). This is Mitchell's most-covered song by far, with over 1,000 versions recorded at latest count.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-covers_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-covers-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hole_(band)" title="Hole (band)">Hole</a> also covered "Both Sides Now" in 1991 on their debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Pretty_on_the_Inside" title="Pretty on the Inside">Pretty on the Inside</a></i>, retitling it "Clouds", with the lyrics altered by frontwoman <a href="/wiki/Courtney_Love" title="Courtney Love">Courtney Love</a>. Pop group <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Neighborhood_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Neighborhood (band) (page does not exist)">Neighborhood</a> in 1970 and <a href="/wiki/Amy_Grant" title="Amy Grant">Amy Grant</a> in 1995 scored hits with covers of "Big Yellow Taxi", the third-most covered song in Mitchell's repertoire (with over 300 covers).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-covers_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-covers-83">[83]</a></sup> Recent releases of this song have been by <a href="/wiki/Counting_Crows" title="Counting Crows">Counting Crows</a> in 2002 and <a href="/wiki/Nena" title="Nena">Nena</a> in 2007. <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> used a sample of the chorus of "Big Yellow Taxi" as the centerpiece of her 1997 hit single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Got_%27Til_It%27s_Gone" title="Got 'Til It's Gone">Got 'Til It's Gone</a>", which also features rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(rapper)" title="Q-Tip (rapper)">Q-Tip</a> saying "Joni Mitchell never lies". "<a href="/wiki/River_(Joni_Mitchell_song)" title="River (Joni Mitchell song)">River</a>", from Mitchell's album <i>Blue</i> became the second-most covered song of Mitchell's in 2013 as many artists chose it for their holiday albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-covers_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-covers-83">[83]</a></sup> Rap artists <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mac_Dre" title="Mac Dre">Mac Dre</a> have also sampled Mitchell's vocals in their music. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a> has covered "Ladies of the Canyon" for the B-side of her 1995 hit "<a href="/wiki/No_More_I_Love_You%27s" title="No More I Love You's">No More I Love You's</a>". <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Moore" title="Mandy Moore">Mandy Moore</a> covered "Help Me" in 2003. In 2004 singer <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> covered her song "Edith and the Kingpin" for a radio show. "River" has been one of the most popular songs covered in recent years, with versions by <a href="/wiki/Dianne_Reeves" title="Dianne Reeves">Dianne Reeves</a> (1999), <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">James Taylor</a> (recorded for television in 2000, and for CD release in 2004), <a href="/wiki/Allison_Crowe" title="Allison Crowe">Allison Crowe</a> (2004), <a href="/wiki/Rachael_Yamagata" title="Rachael Yamagata">Rachael Yamagata</a> (2004), <a href="/wiki/Aimee_Mann" title="Aimee Mann">Aimee Mann</a> (2005), and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_McLachlan" title="Sarah McLachlan">Sarah McLachlan</a> (2006). McLachlan also did a version of "Blue" in 1996, and <a href="/wiki/Cat_Power" title="Cat Power">Cat Power</a> recorded a cover of "Blue" in 2008. Other Mitchell covers include the famous "<a href="/wiki/Woodstock_(song)" title="Woodstock (song)">Woodstock</a>" by both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crosby,_Stills_%26_Nash_(and_Young)" title="Crosby, Stills &amp; Nash (and Young)">Crosby, Stills, Nash and Young</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthews_Southern_Comfort" title="Matthews Southern Comfort">Matthews Southern Comfort</a>, "This Flight Tonight" by <a href="/wiki/Nazareth_(band)" title="Nazareth (band)">Nazareth</a>, and well-known versions of "Woodstock" by <a href="/wiki/Eva_Cassidy" title="Eva Cassidy">Eva Cassidy</a> and "A Case of You" by <a href="/wiki/Tori_Amos" title="Tori Amos">Tori Amos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Branch" title="Michelle Branch">Michelle Branch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Monheit" title="Jane Monheit">Jane Monheit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diana_Krall" title="Diana Krall">Diana Krall</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Blake_(musician)" title="James Blake (musician)">James Blake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ana_Moura" title="Ana Moura">Ana Moura</a>. A 40th anniversary version of "Woodstock" was released in 2009 by Nick Vernier Band featuring Ian Matthews (formerly of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthews_Southern_Comfort" title="Matthews Southern Comfort">Matthews Southern Comfort</a>). Fellow Canadian singer <a href="/wiki/K.d._lang" title="K.d. lang">k.d. lang</a> recorded two of Mitchell's songs ("A Case of You" and "Jericho") for her 2004 album <i><a href="/wiki/Hymns_of_the_49th_Parallel" title="Hymns of the 49th Parallel">Hymns of the 49th Parallel</a></i> which is composed entirely of songs written by Canadian artists.</p>
<p>Prince's version of "A Case of U" appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/A_Tribute_to_Joni_Mitchell" title="A Tribute to Joni Mitchell">A Tribute to Joni Mitchell</a></i>, a 2007 compilation released by <a href="/wiki/Nonesuch_Records" title="Nonesuch Records">Nonesuch Records</a>, which also featured <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rk" title="Björk">Björk</a> ("The Boho Dance"), <a href="/wiki/Caetano_Veloso" title="Caetano Veloso">Caetano Veloso</a> ("Dreamland"), <a href="/wiki/Emmylou_Harris" title="Emmylou Harris">Emmylou Harris</a> ("The Magdalene Laundries"), <a href="/wiki/Sufjan_Stevens" title="Sufjan Stevens">Sufjan Stevens</a> ("Free Man in Paris") and <a href="/wiki/Cassandra_Wilson" title="Cassandra Wilson">Cassandra Wilson</a> ("For the Roses"), among others.</p>
<p>Several other songs reference Joni Mitchell. The song "<a href="/wiki/Our_House_(Crosby,_Stills,_Nash_%26_Young_song)" title="Our House (Crosby, Stills, Nash &amp; Young song)">Our House</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Graham_Nash" title="Graham Nash">Graham Nash</a> refers to Nash's two-year affair with Mitchell at the time that Crosby, Stills, Nash and Young recorded the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9j%C3%A0_Vu_(Crosby,_Stills,_Nash_%26_Young_album)" title="Déjà Vu (Crosby, Stills, Nash &amp; Young album)">Déjà Vu</a> album. <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Going_to_California" title="Going to California">Going to California</a>" was said to be written about <a href="/wiki/Robert_Plant" title="Robert Plant">Robert Plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Limerence" title="Limerence">infatuation</a> with Mitchell, a claim that seems to be borne out by the fact that, in live performances, Plant often says "Joni" after the line "To find a queen without a king, they say she plays guitar and cries and sings". Jimmy Page uses a double dropped D guitar tuning similar to the alternative tunings Mitchell uses. The <a href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth" title="Sonic Youth">Sonic Youth</a> song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hey_Joni" title="Hey Joni">Hey Joni</a>" is named for Mitchell. <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a> also mentions Mitchell in one of her songs, "Your House". British folk singer <a href="/wiki/Frank_Turner" title="Frank Turner">Frank Turner</a> mentions Mitchell in his song "Sunshine State". The <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a> song "The Ballad of Dorothy Parker" contains the lyric – " 'Oh, my favorite song' she said – and it was Joni singing 'Help me I think I'm falling' ". "<a href="/wiki/Lavender_(Marillion_song)" title="Lavender (Marillion song)">Lavender</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Marillion" title="Marillion">Marillion</a> was partly influenced by "going through parks listening to Joni Mitchell", according to vocalist and lyricist <a href="/wiki/Fish_(singer)" title="Fish (singer)">Fish</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and she was later mentioned in the lyrics of their song "Montreal" from <i><a href="/wiki/Sounds_That_Can%27t_Be_Made" title="Sounds That Can't Be Made">Sounds That Can't Be Made</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a> makes reference to Mitchell and her <i>Blue</i> album in his song "<a href="/wiki/Queen_of_California" title="Queen of California">Queen of California</a>", from his 2012 album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_and_Raised_(John_Mayer_album)" title="Born and Raised (John Mayer album)">Born and Raised</a></i>. The song contains the lyric "Joni wrote <i>Blue</i> in a house by the sea".</p>
<p>In 2003, playwright <a href="/wiki/Bryden_MacDonald" title="Bryden MacDonald">Bryden MacDonald</a> launched <i>When All the Slaves Are Free</i>, a musical revue based on Mitchell's music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-columbia_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-columbia-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mitchell's music and poems have deeply influenced the French painter <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Benoit" title="Jacques Benoit">Jacques Benoit</a>'s work. Between 1979 and 1989 Benoit produced sixty paintings, corresponding to a selection of fifty of Mitchell's songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maynard_James_Keenan" title="Maynard James Keenan">Maynard James Keenan</a> of the American <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Tool_(band)" title="Tool (band)">Tool</a> has cited Mitchell as an influence, claiming that her influence is what allows him to "soften [staccato, rhythmic, insane mathematical paths] and bring [them] back to the center, so you can listen to it without having an eye-ache."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Joni_Mitchell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Awards and honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1957" data-file-width="2295" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/220px-Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/330px-Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/440px-Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joni_Mitchell_Star_on_Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Joni Mitchell's star on <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada's Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mitchell's home country of Canada has bestowed several honours on her. She was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Music Hall of Fame">Canadian Music Hall of Fame</a> in 1981 and received the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_General%27s_Performing_Arts_Award" title="Governor General's Performing Arts Award">Governor General's Performing Arts Award</a> for Lifetime Artistic Achievement, Canada's highest honour in the performing arts, in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Mitchell received a star on Canada's Walk of Fame in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In 2002 she became only the third popular Canadian singer/songwriter (<a href="/wiki/Gordon_Lightfoot" title="Gordon Lightfoot">Gordon Lightfoot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cohen" title="Leonard Cohen">Leonard Cohen</a> being the other two), to be appointed a Companion of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a>, Canada's highest civilian honour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jm-ooc-2002_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-jm-ooc-2002-91">[91]</a></sup> She received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honorary_doctorate" title="Honorary doctorate">honorary doctorate</a> in music from <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> in 2004. In January 2007 she was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Songwriters Hall of Fame">Canadian Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>. In June 2007 <a href="/wiki/Canada_Post" title="Canada Post">Canada Post</a> featured Mitchell on a postage stamp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mitchell has received nine Grammy Awards during her career (eight competitive, one honorary), the first in 1969 and the most recent in 2016. She received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a> in 2002, with the citation describing her as "one of the most important female recording artists of the rock era" and "a powerful influence on all artists who embrace diversity, imagination and integrity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, Mitchell received Billboard's Century Award. In 1996, she was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Polar_Music_Prize" title="Polar Music Prize">Polar Music Prize</a>. In 1997, Mitchell was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>, but did not attend the ceremony.</p>
<p>In tribute to Mitchell, the <a href="/wiki/TNT_(TV_channel)" title="TNT (TV channel)">TNT network</a> presented an all-star celebration at the <a href="/wiki/Hammerstein_Ballroom" title="Hammerstein Ballroom">Hammerstein Ballroom</a> in New York City on April 6, 2000. Mitchell's songs were sung by many performers, including James Taylor, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wynonna_Judd" title="Wynonna Judd">Wynonna Judd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diana_Krall" title="Diana Krall">Diana Krall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Thompson_(musician)" title="Richard Thompson (musician)">Richard Thompson</a>. Mitchell herself ended the evening with a rendition of "Both Sides Now" with a 70-piece orchestra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The version was featured on the soundtrack to the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Actually" title="Love Actually">Love Actually</a></i>.</p>
<p>On February 12, 2010, "<a href="/wiki/Both_Sides,_Now" title="Both Sides, Now">Both Sides, Now</a>" was performed at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2010 Winter Olympics opening ceremony">2010 Winter Olympics opening ceremony</a> in Vancouver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>To celebrate Mitchell's 70th birthday, the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Luminato" title="Luminato">Luminato</a> Festival in Toronto held a set of tribute concerts entitled <i>Joni: A Portrait in Song – A Birthday Happening Live</i> at <a href="/wiki/Massey_Hall" title="Massey Hall">Massey Hall</a> on June 18 and 19. Performers included <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Wainwright" title="Rufus Wainwright">Rufus Wainwright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbie_Hancock" title="Herbie Hancock">Herbie Hancock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esperanza_Spalding" title="Esperanza Spalding">Esperanza Spalding</a>, and rare performances by Mitchell herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to health problems she could not attend the San Francisco gala in May 2015 to receive the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SFJAZZ" title="SFJAZZ">SFJAZZ</a> Lifetime Achievement Award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, Mitchell was ranked 42nd on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)"><i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s</a> "100 greatest singers" list and in 2015 she was ranked ninth on their list of "The 100 greatest songwriters of all time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Joni_Mitchell&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tower-wireless-can.png"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="507" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Tower-wireless-can.png/24px-Tower-wireless-can.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Tower-wireless-can.png/36px-Tower-wireless-can.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/Tower-wireless-can.png/48px-Tower-wireless-can.png 2x" width="24"/></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Music_of_Canada" title="Portal:Music of Canada">Music of Canada portal</a></span></li>
